 MCP Z3 AGENT - Symbolic Reasoning

### Query
# Problem Statement Find all stable matchings between 40 residents and 20 hospitals where each

hospital has a capacity limit and both residents and hospitals have strict preference rankings over
acceptable partners. ## Instance Data **Residents:** r1, r2, ..., r40 (40 total) **Hospitals and
Capacities:** - h1: 2, h2: 2, h3: 2, h4: 2, h5: 2, h6: 2 - h7: 4, h8: 3, h9: 1 - h10: 3, h11: 3,
h12: 2 - h13: 3, h14: 3, h15: 2 - h16: 2, h17: 2 - h18: 1, h19: 1, h20: 1 (no acceptable residents)
**Resident Preferences** (only acceptable hospitals listed, in order of preference): Block A1
(r1-r4): - r1: h1 > h2 - r2: h1 > h2 - r3: h2 > h1 - r4: h2 > h1 Block A2 (r5-r8): - r5: h3 > h4 -
r6: h3 > h4 - r7: h4 > h3 - r8: h4 > h3 Block A3 (r9-r12): - r9: h5 > h6 - r10: h5 > h6 - r11: h6 >
h5 - r12: h6 > h5 Block B1 (r13-r20): - r13: h7 > h8 > h9 - r14: h7 > h8 > h9 - r15: h8 > h7 > h9 -
r16: h8 > h7 > h9 - r17: h7 > h8 > h9 - r18: h7 > h9 > h8 - r19: h8 > h9 > h7 - r20: h9 > h8 > h7
Block B2 (r21-r28): - r21: h10 > h11 > h12 - r22: h10 > h12 > h11 - r23: h11 > h10 > h12 - r24: h11
> h12 > h10 - r25: h10 > h11 > h12 - r26: h11 > h10 > h12 - r27: h12 > h11 > h10 - r28: h12 > h10 >
h11 Block B3 (r29-r36): - r29: h13 > h14 > h15 - r30: h13 > h15 > h14 - r31: h14 > h13 > h15 - r32:
h14 > h15 > h13 - r33: h13 > h14 > h15 - r34: h14 > h13 > h15 - r35: h15 > h14 > h13 - r36: h15 >
h13 > h14 Block A4 (r37-r40): - r37: h16 > h17 - r38: h16 > h17 - r39: h17 > h16 - r40: h17 > h16
**Hospital Preferences** (only acceptable residents listed, in order of preference): Block A1: - h1:
r3 > r4 > r1 > r2 - h2: r1 > r2 > r3 > r4 Block A2: - h3: r7 > r8 > r5 > r6 - h4: r5 > r6 > r7 > r8
Block A3: - h5: r11 > r12 > r9 > r10 - h6: r9 > r10 > r11 > r12 Block B1: - h7: r13 > r14 > r17 >
r18 > r15 > r16 > r19 > r20 - h8: r15 > r16 > r19 > r13 > r14 > r17 > r18 > r20 - h9: r20 > r19 >
r18 > r17 > r16 > r15 > r14 > r13 Block B2: - h10: r21 > r22 > r25 > r23 > r24 > r26 > r27 > r28 -
h11: r23 > r24 > r26 > r21 > r22 > r25 > r27 > r28 - h12: r27 > r28 > r23 > r24 > r21 > r22 > r25 >
r26 Block B3: - h13: r29 > r30 > r33 > r31 > r32 > r34 > r35 > r36 - h14: r31 > r32 > r34 > r29 >
r30 > r33 > r35 > r36 - h15: r35 > r36 > r31 > r32 > r29 > r30 > r33 > r34 Block A4: - h16: r39 >
r40 > r37 > r38 - h17: r37 > r38 > r39 > r40 Hospitals h18, h19, h20: no acceptable residents
(remain empty) ## Constraints 1. Each **resident** must be matched to at most one hospital 2. Each
**hospital** must be matched to at most its capacity of residents 3. Only **mutually acceptable**
pairs can be matched (both must appear in each other's preference list) 4. **Stability**: No
blocking pair (r, h) where: - r prefers h over their current assignment (or is unmatched), AND - h
would accept r (either has free capacity OR prefers r over at least one current assignee) ##
Objective Find all stable matchings that satisfy the constraints. ## Expected Result This instance
has exactly 81 stable matchings. The problem decomposes into independent blocks: - Blocks A1, A2,
A3, A4 each have 3 stable matchings - Blocks B1, B2, B3 each have 1 unique stable matching - Total:
3 × 3 × 3 × 3 = 81 stable matchings ## Output Format The solution must be a JSON object with the
following structure: ```json { "stable_matchings": [ [ ["r1", "h1"], ["r2", "h2"], ... ], [ ["r1",
"h2"], ["r2", "h1"], ... ] ], "count": 81 } ``` **Fields:** - **stable_matchings**: List of all
stable matchings, where each matching is a list of [resident, hospital] pairs - **count**: Total
number of stable matchings found

  - write_and_run_z3: Write Python code using Z3 to a file and run it immediately to get results.
We capture printed stdout and stderr from running the script.

- Let me analyze this problem carefully. This is a Hospital-Resident matching problem with capacities, and I need to find ALL stable matchings.

- Let me write a Z3 script that: 1. Encodes the matching problem 2. Finds all stable matchings by enumeration 3. Prints the count
- For stability, I need to encode: no blocking pair exists. A blocking pair (r, h) is one where: - r prefers h over their current assignment (or is unmatched) - h would accept r (has free capacity OR prefers r over at least one current assignee)
- Let me think about how to encode this efficiently.
- For each resident r, let `match[r]` be the hospital they're matched to (or 0 for unmatched). For each hospital h, let `assigned[h]` be the set of residents assigned to h.
- Actually, let me use a different encoding. For each resident r and hospital h, let `assigned[r][h]` be a Bool indicating whether r is matched to h.
- Constraints: 1. Each resident matched to at most one hospital: For each r, sum of assigned[r][h] over h <= 1 2. Each hospital matched to at most capacity: For each h, sum of assigned[r][h] over r <= capacity[h] 3. Only mutually acceptable pairs: assigned[r][h] can only be true if h is in r's preference list and r is in h's preference list 4. Stability: No blocking pair
- For stability, I need to define "r prefers h over current assignment" and "h would accept r".
- Let me define preference ranks. For each resident r, pref_rank_r[h] = position of h in r's preference list (lower = more preferred). If h is not in r's list, pref_rank = infinity.
- Similarly for hospitals.
- A blocking pair (r, h) exists if: - h is acceptable to r (in r's preference list) - r is acceptable to h (in h's preference list) - Either r is unmatched, or r prefers h over current match (pref_rank_r[h] < pref_rank_r[current_match]) - Either h has free capacity, or h prefers r over at least one current assignee
- For the stability constraint, I need: for all acceptable pairs (r, h), NOT a blocking pair.
- Let me think about this more carefully. For each acceptable pair (r, h): - If r is matched to h, it's not a blocking pair (they're already matched) - If r is matched to some h' where r prefers h' over h, not a blocking pair - If h is at capacity and all current assignees are preferred over r by h, not a blocking pair - Otherwise, it IS a blocking pair
- So the stability constraint is: for each acceptable pair (r, h) where r is NOT matched to h: - Either r prefers their current match over h, OR - h is at capacity AND h prefers all current assignees over r
- Let me encode this.
- Actually, let me think about the encoding more carefully.
- For each resident r, I'll use an integer variable `match_r` representing the hospital they're matched to (0 = unmatched, 1-20 = hospital index).
- For each hospital h, I need to track which residents are assigned. I can use Bool variables `assigned[r][h]` for each resident-hospital pair.
- Let me use the `assigned[r][h]` approach since it makes stability checking easier.
- For the preference ranks, I'll precompute them as constants.
- Let me write the code:
- ```python from z3 import *
- # Define residents and hospitals residents = list(range(1, 41))  # r1 to r40 hospitals = list(range(1, 21))  # h1 to h20
- # Hospital capacities capacity = { 1: 2, 2: 2, 3: 2, 4: 2, 5: 2, 6: 2, 7: 4, 8: 3, 9: 1, 10: 3, 11: 3, 12: 2, 13: 3, 14: 3, 15: 2, 16: 2, 17: 2, 18: 1, 19: 1, 20: 1 }

- Now I need to compute preference ranks. For resident r, `res_rank[r][h]` = position (0-indexed) of h in r's preference list, or a large number if not acceptable.
- For hospital h, `hosp_rank[h][r]` = position (0-indexed) of r in h's preference list, or a large number if not acceptable.
- For stability, for each acceptable pair (r, h): - If r is matched to h, not a blocking pair - If r is matched to h' where res_rank[r][h'] < res_rank[r][h], not a blocking pair - If h is at capacity AND for all r' assigned to h, hosp_rank[h][r'] < hosp_rank[h][r], not a blocking pair - Otherwise, it IS a blocking pair
- The stability constraint: for all acceptable pairs (r, h), NOT a blocking pair.
- Let me think about how to encode "r prefers current match over h" when r might be unmatched.
- If r is unmatched, then r prefers any acceptable hospital over being unmatched. So "r prefers current match over h" is false if r is unmatched.
- Let me use `assigned[r][h]` as Bool variables.
- For each acceptable pair (r, h), the blocking pair condition is: - Not assigned to h: Not(assigned[r][h]) - r prefers h over current match: For all h' that r is assigned to, res_rank[r][h] < res_rank[r][h']. Since r can be assigned to at most one hospital, this is: either r is unmatched, or r is assigned to some h' where res_rank[r][h] < res_rank[r][h']. - r is unmatched: And([Not(assigned[r][hp]) for hp in res_prefs[r]]) - r prefers h over current: Or([And(assigned[r][hp], res_rank[r][h] < res_rank[r][hp]) for hp in res_prefs[r] if res_rank[r][h] < res_rank[r][hp]]) - Combined: Or(r_unmatched, r_prefers_h_over_current)
- - h would accept r: Either h has free capacity, or h prefers r over at least one current assignee. - h has free capacity: Sum([assigned[rp][h] for rp in residents if h in res_prefs.get(rp, [])]) < capacity[h] - h prefers r over some assignee: Or([And(assigned[rp][h], hosp_rank[h][r] < hosp_rank[h][rp]) for rp in hosp_prefs[h] if hosp_rank[h][r] < hosp_rank[h][rp]]) - Combined: Or(h_free_capacity, h_prefers_r_over_someone)
- So the blocking pair condition for (r, h) is: And(Not(assigned[r][h]), Or(r_unmatched, r_prefers_h_over_current), Or(h_free_capacity, h_prefers_r_over_someone))
- And the stability constraint is: for all acceptable pairs (r, h), NOT this condition.
- This is going to be a lot of constraints but should work.

- Wait, but 81 solutions with blocking clauses means 81 solver calls. Each call adds a blocking clause. For a problem of this size, it should be manageable.
- Let me write the full script.
- Actually, let me think about this differently. Since the blocks are independent, I can: 1. For each block, find all stable matchings 2. The total count is the product of counts
- This is much more efficient. Let me write a function that solves one block.
- Let me write the code step by step.
- ```python from z3 import *
- def solve_block(block_name, res_list, hosp_list, cap, res_prefs_block, hosp_prefs_block): """Find all stable matchings for a block.""" solver = Solver()
- # Decision variables: assigned[r][h] = True if resident r is assigned to hospital h assigned = {} for r in res_list: for h in hosp_list: assigned[(r, h)] = Bool(f'assigned_{r}_{h}')
- # Constraint 1: Each resident matched to at most one hospital for r in res_list: acceptable_hosps = res_prefs_block.get(r, []) solver.add(Sum([If(assigned[(r, h)], 1, 0) for h in acceptable_hosps]) <= 1)
- # Constraint 2: Each hospital matched to at most its capacity for h in hosp_list: acceptable_res = hosp_prefs_block.get(h, []) solver.add(Sum([If(assigned[(r, h)], 1, 0) for r in acceptable_res]) <= cap[h])
- # Constraint 3: Only mutually acceptable pairs # Build set of acceptable pairs acceptable_pairs = set() for r in res_list: for h in res_prefs_block.get(r, []): if r in hosp_prefs_block.get(h, []): acceptable_pairs.add((r, h))
- for r in res_list: for h in hosp_list: if (r, h) not in acceptable_pairs: solver.add(Not(assigned[(r, h)]))
- # Compute preference ranks res_rank = {} for r in res_list: for i, h in enumerate(res_prefs_block.get(r, [])): res_rank[(r, h)] = i
- hosp_rank = {} for h in hosp_list: for i, r in enumerate(hosp_prefs_block.get(h, [])): hosp_rank[(h, r)] = i
- # Constraint 4: Stability - no blocking pairs for (r, h) in acceptable_pairs: # Check if (r, h) is a blocking pair # r prefers h over current match (or is unmatched) r_unmatched = And([Not(assigned[(r, hp)]) for hp in res_prefs_block.get(r, [])])
- r_prefers_h = [] for hp in res_prefs_block.get(r, []): if res_rank.get((r, h), 999) < res_rank.get((r, hp), 999): r_prefers_h.append(And(assigned[(r, hp)], True))  # r is assigned to hp and prefers h # Wait, this is wrong. I need: r is assigned to hp AND h is preferred over hp # res_rank[(r,h)] < res_rank[(r,hp)] means r prefers h over hp pass
- # Actually let me redo this # r_prefers_h_over_current: r is assigned to some hp where r prefers h over hp r_prefers_h_over_current_parts = [] for hp in res_prefs_block.get(r, []): if res_rank.get((r, h), 999) < res_rank.get((r, hp), 999): r_prefers_h_over_current_parts.append(assigned[(r, hp)])
- r_wants_h = Or(r_unmatched, Or(r_prefers_h_over_current_parts)) if r_prefers_h_over_current_parts else r_unmatched
- # h would accept r: either h has free capacity, or h prefers r over at least one current assignee h_acceptable_res = hosp_prefs_block.get(h, []) h_current_count = Sum([If(assigned[(rp, h)], 1, 0) for rp in h_acceptable_res]) h_has_capacity = h_current_count < cap[h]
- h_prefers_r_over_someone_parts = [] for rp in hosp_prefs_block.get(h, []): if hosp_rank.get((h, r), 999) < hosp_rank.get((h, rp), 999): h_prefers_r_over_someone_parts.append(assigned[(rp, h)])
- h_would_accept = Or(h_has_capacity, Or(h_prefers_r_over_someone_parts)) if h_prefers_r_over_someone_parts else h_has_capacity
- # Not a blocking pair: either r doesn't want h, or h wouldn't accept r solver.add(Or(Not(r_wants_h), Not(h_would_accept)))
- # Enumerate all solutions solutions = [] decision_vars = [assigned[(r, h)] for (r, h) in acceptable_pairs]
- while solver.check() == sat: m = solver.model() sol = {} for r in res_list: for h in res_prefs_block.get(r, []): if (r, h) in acceptable_pairs: val = m.evaluate(assigned[(r, h)], model_completion=True) if is_true(val): sol[r] = h solutions.append(sol)
- # Block this solution blocking = [] for r in res_list: matched_h = sol.get(r) for h in res_prefs_block.get(r, []): if (r, h) in acceptable_pairs: if matched_h == h: blocking.append(assigned[(r, h)]) else: blocking.append(Not(assigned[(r, h)])) solver.add(Not(And(blocking)))
- return solutions ```
- Hmm, this is getting complex. Let me simplify and write a cleaner version.
- Actually, let me think about the blocking clause more carefully. The decision variables are `assigned[(r, h)]` for each acceptable pair. To block a solution, I need to ensure at least one of these variables differs.
- For the blocking clause, I can use: ```python solver.add(Or([v != m.evaluate(v, model_completion=True) for v in decision_vars])) ```
- But this might be slow for many variables. Let me use a more targeted approach.
- Actually, for the blocking clause, I should only use the variables that are True in the solution (the matched pairs). If I block based on all variables, it should work but might be less efficient.
- Let me just use the standard approach: ```python blocking_clause = Or([v != m.evaluate(v, model_completion=True) for v in decision_vars]) solver.add(blocking_clause) ```
- Wait, but `m.evaluate(v, model_completion=True)` returns a Z3 Bool value. The comparison `v != z3_bool_value` should work.
- Actually, let me think about this differently. For each resident r, I can define `match[r]` as an Int variable representing the hospital they're matched to (0 = unmatched). Then the blocking clause is simpler: at least one resident must have a different match.
- Let me use Int variables for matching:
- ```python match = {} for r in res_list: match[r] = Int(f'match_{r}') # Domain: 0 (unmatched) or one of the acceptable hospitals solver.add(Or([match[r] == 0] + [match[r] == h for h in res_prefs_block.get(r, [])])) ```
- Then for capacity: ```python for h in hosp_list: solver.add(Sum([If(match[r] == h, 1, 0) for r in hosp_prefs_block.get(h, [])]) <= cap[h]) ```
- For stability, I need to check for each acceptable pair (r, h): - r prefers h over current match: match[r] == 0 OR res_rank[(r, h)] < res_rank[(r, match[r])] - h would accept r: h has free capacity OR h prefers r over at least one current assignee
- The tricky part is "res_rank[(r, h)] < res_rank[(r, match[r])]" because match[r] is symbolic.
- I can encode this as: ```python # r prefers h over current match r_prefers_h = Or( match[r] == 0, Or([And(match[r] == hp, res_rank[(r, h)] < res_rank[(r, hp)]) for hp in res_prefs_block.get(r, []) if res_rank[(r, h)] < res_rank.get((r, hp), 999)]) ) ```
- For "h prefers r over at least one current assignee": ```python h_prefers_r = Or([And(match[rp] == h, hosp_rank[(h, r)] < hosp_rank[(h, rp)]) for rp in hosp_prefs_block.get(h, []) if hosp_rank[(h, r)] < hosp_rank.get((h, rp), 999)]) ```
- For "h has free capacity": ```python h_has_capacity = Sum([If(match[rp] == h, 1, 0) for rp in hosp_prefs_block.get(h, [])]) < cap[h] ```
- This approach with Int variables is cleaner. Let me write the full script.
- Actually, I realize I should be more careful. The problem says "each resident must be matched to at most one hospital" and "each hospital must be matched to at most its capacity". So residents can be unmatched and hospitals can have fewer than capacity.
- Also, the problem says "only mutually acceptable pairs can be matched". So I need to ensure that if match[r] == h, then h is in r's preference list AND r is in h's preference list.
- Let me write the complete script now.
- Actually, let me think about whether to solve each block independently or the whole problem at once. Since the blocks are independent, solving each block separately is much more efficient. Let me do that.
- Let me write a function that takes a block's data and returns all stable matchings for that block.
- ```python from z3 import *
- def find_stable_matchings(block_name, res_list, hosp_list, cap, res_prefs_block, hosp_prefs_block): """Find all stable matchings for a block.""" solver = Solver()
- # Decision variables match = {} for r in res_list: match[r] = Int(f'match_{r}') acceptable = res_prefs_block.get(r, []) solver.add(Or([match[r] == 0] + [match[r] == h for h in acceptable]))
- # Capacity constraints for h in hosp_list: acceptable_res = hosp_prefs_block.get(h, []) solver.add(Sum([If(match[r] == h, 1, 0) for r in acceptable_res]) <= cap[h])
- # Compute preference ranks res_rank = {} for r in res_list: for i, h in enumerate(res_prefs_block.get(r, [])): res_rank[(r, h)] = i
- hosp_rank = {} for h in hosp_list: for i, r in enumerate(hosp_prefs_block.get(h, [])): hosp_rank[(h, r)] = i
- # Build acceptable pairs acceptable_pairs = set() for r in res_list: for h in res_prefs_block.get(r, []): if r in hosp_prefs_block.get(h, []): acceptable_pairs.add((r, h))
- # Stability constraints for (r, h) in acceptable_pairs: # r prefers h over current match (or is unmatched) r_prefers_parts = [] for hp in res_prefs_block.get(r, []): if res_rank[(r, h)] < res_rank.get((r, hp), 999): r_prefers_parts.append(match[r] == hp) r_prefers_h = Or([match[r] == 0] + r_prefers_parts)
- # h would accept r h_acceptable_res = hosp_prefs_block.get(h, []) h_has_capacity = Sum([If(match[rp] == h, 1, 0) for rp in h_acceptable_res]) < cap[h]
- h_prefers_parts = [] for rp in hosp_prefs_block.get(h, []): if hosp_rank[(h, r)] < hosp_rank.get((h, rp), 999): h_prefers_parts.append(match[rp] == h) h_prefers_r = Or(h_prefers_parts) if h_prefers_parts else False
- h_would_accept = Or(h_has_capacity, h_prefers_r) if h_prefers_parts else h_has_capacity
- # Not a blocking pair solver.add(Or(Not(r_prefers_h), Not(h_would_accept)))
- # Enumerate all solutions solutions = [] decision_vars = [match[r] for r in res_list]
- while solver.check() == sat: m = solver.model() sol = {} for r in res_list: val = m.evaluate(match[r], model_completion=True) sol[r] = int(str(val)) solutions.append(sol)
- # Block this solution solver.add(Or([match[r] != sol[r] for r in res_list]))
- return solutions ```
- Wait, I need to be careful with the `h_would_accept` when `h_prefers_parts` is empty. If h has no residents it prefers less than r, then h_prefers_r is False, and h_would_accept is just h_has_capacity.
- Actually, let me reconsider. `h_prefers_r` should be "h prefers r over at least one current assignee". If `h_prefers_parts` is empty, it means there's no resident in h's preference list that h likes less than r. So h_prefers_r is False.
- But wait, `h_prefers_parts` contains `match[rp] == h` for residents rp that h prefers less than r. If this list is empty, it means r is the least preferred resident (or not in the list at all). In that case, h would only accept r if there's free capacity.
- Actually, I need to be more careful. `h_prefers_parts` is empty when there's no rp in h's preference list such that hosp_rank[(h, r)] < hosp_rank[(h, rp)]. This means r is at the bottom of h's preference list (or there are no residents below r). In this case, h_prefers_r should be False (h doesn't prefer r over any current assignee).
- So `h_would_accept = h_has_capacity` in this case. That's correct.
- But what if `h_prefers_parts` is non-empty? Then `h_prefers_r = Or(h_prefers_parts)`. And `h_would_accept = Or(h_has_capacity, h_prefers_r)`.
- Wait, but `h_prefers_r` being True means there exists some rp assigned to h that h prefers less than r. But this doesn't mean h would actually accept r - it means h would rather have r than rp. So if h is at capacity and prefers r over some current assignee, h would accept r (by dropping the less preferred assignee).
- Actually, in the standard hospital-resident matching stability definition: - A blocking pair (r, h) exists if: 1. r is acceptable to h AND h is acceptable to r 2. Either r is unmatched or r prefers h to their current match 3. Either h is under capacity or h prefers r to at least one of its current assignees
- So condition 3 is: h has free capacity OR h prefers r over at least one current assignee.
- My encoding seems correct. Let me continue.
- Let me now write the complete script that solves each block and combines the results.
- Actually, I realize I should double-check the acceptable pairs. In this problem, the preference lists define acceptability. So if r lists h in their preferences, h is acceptable to r. And if h lists r in their preferences, r is acceptable to h. A pair is mutually acceptable only if both conditions hold.
- Looking at the data: - Block A1: r1-r4 all list h1 and/or h2. h1 lists r1-r4, h2 lists r1-r4. So all pairs within {r1,r2,r3,r4} × {h1,h2} are mutually acceptable. - Similarly for other blocks.

- Actually, for the final output, I need to print all 81 stable matchings. That's a lot of output. Let me think about how to format this.
- The problem says: - **stable_matchings**: List of all stable matchings, where each matching is a list of [resident, hospital] pairs - **count**: Total number of stable matchings found
- So I need to enumerate all 81 matchings. Each matching is a combination of one matching from each block.
- Let me write the script:
- ```python from z3 import * from itertools import product
- def find_block_matchings(block_name, res_list, hosp_list, cap, res_prefs_block, hosp_prefs_block): """Find all stable matchings for a block.""" solver = Solver()
- match = {} for r in res_list: match[r] = Int(f'match_{r}') acceptable = res_prefs_block.get(r, []) solver.add(Or([match[r] == 0] + [match[r] == h for h in acceptable]))
- for h in hosp_list: acceptable_res = hosp_prefs_block.get(h, []) solver.add(Sum([If(match[r] == h, 1, 0) for r in acceptable_res]) <= cap[h])
- res_rank = {} for r in res_list: for i, h in enumerate(res_prefs_block.get(r, [])): res_rank[(r, h)] = i
- hosp_rank = {} for h in hosp_list: for i, r in enumerate(hosp_prefs_block.get(h, [])): hosp_rank[(h, r)] = i
- acceptable_pairs = set() for r in res_list: for h in res_prefs_block.get(r, []): if r in hosp_prefs_block.get(h, []): acceptable_pairs.add((r, h))
- for (r, h) in acceptable_pairs: r_prefers_parts = [] for hp in res_prefs_block.get(r, []): if res_rank[(r, h)] < res_rank.get((r, hp), 999): r_prefers_parts.append(match[r] == hp) r_prefers_h = Or([match[r] == 0] + r_prefers_parts)
- h_acceptable_res = hosp_prefs_block.get(h, []) h_has_capacity = Sum([If(match[rp] == h, 1, 0) for rp in h_acceptable_res]) < cap[h]
- h_prefers_parts = [] for rp in hosp_prefs_block.get(h, []): if hosp_rank[(h, r)] < hosp_rank.get((h, rp), 999): h_prefers_parts.append(match[rp] == h)
- if h_prefers_parts: h_would_accept = Or(h_has_capacity, Or(h_prefers_parts)) else: h_would_accept = h_has_capacity
- solver.add(Or(Not(r_prefers_h), Not(h_would_accept)))
- solutions = [] while solver.check() == sat: m = solver.model() sol = {} for r in res_list: val = m.evaluate(match[r], model_completion=True) sol[r] = int(str(val)) solutions.append(sol) solver.add(Or([match[r] != sol[r] for r in res_list]))
- return solutions
- # Define data capacity = { 1: 2, 2: 2, 3: 2, 4: 2, 5: 2, 6: 2, 7: 4, 8: 3, 9: 1, 10: 3, 11: 3, 12: 2, 13: 3, 14: 3, 15: 2, 16: 2, 17: 2, 18: 1, 19: 1, 20: 1 }
- # Block definitions blocks = { 'A1': { 'res': [1, 2, 3, 4], 'hosp': [1, 2], 'res_prefs': { 1: [1, 2], 2: [1, 2], 3: [2, 1], 4: [2, 1] }, 'hosp_prefs': { 1: [3, 4, 1, 2], 2: [1, 2, 3, 4] } }, 'A2': { 'res': [5, 6, 7, 8], 'hosp': [3, 4], 'res_prefs': { 5: [3, 4], 6: [3, 4], 7: [4, 3], 8: [4, 3] }, 'hosp_prefs': { 3: [7, 8, 5, 6], 4: [5, 6, 7, 8] } }, 'A3': { 'res': [9, 10, 11, 12], 'hosp': [5, 6], 'res_prefs': { 9: [5, 6], 10: [5, 6], 11: [6, 5], 12: [6, 5] }, 'hosp_prefs': { 5: [11, 12, 9, 10], 6: [9, 10, 11, 12] } }, 'A4': { 'res': [37, 38, 39, 40], 'hosp': [16, 17], 'res_prefs': { 37: [16, 17], 38: [16, 17], 39: [17, 16], 40: [17, 16] }, 'hosp_prefs': { 16: [39, 40, 37, 38], 17: [37, 38, 39, 40] } }, 'B1': { 'res': [13, 14, 15, 16, 17, 18, 19, 20], 'hosp': [7, 8, 9], 'res_prefs': { 13: [7, 8, 9], 14: [7, 8, 9], 15: [8, 7, 9], 16: [8, 7, 9], 17: [7, 8, 9], 18: [7, 9, 8], 19: [8, 9, 7], 20: [9, 8, 7] }, 'hosp_prefs': { 7: [13, 14, 17, 18, 15, 16, 19, 20], 8: [15, 16, 19, 13, 14, 17, 18, 20], 9: [20, 19, 18, 17, 16, 15, 14, 13] } }, 'B2': { 'res': [21, 22, 23, 24, 25, 26, 27, 28], 'hosp': [10, 11, 12], 'res_prefs': { 21: [10, 11, 12], 22: [10, 12, 11], 23: [11, 10, 12], 24: [11, 12, 10], 25: [10, 11, 12], 26: [11, 10, 12], 27: [12, 11, 10], 28: [12, 10, 11] }, 'hosp_prefs': { 10: [21, 22, 25, 23, 24, 26, 27, 28], 11: [23, 24, 26, 21, 22, 25, 27, 28], 12: [27, 28, 23, 24, 21, 22, 25, 26] } }, 'B3': { 'res': [29, 30, 31, 32, 33, 34, 35, 36], 'hosp': [13, 14, 15], 'res_prefs': { 29: [13, 14, 15], 30: [13, 15, 14], 31: [14, 13, 15], 32: [14, 15, 13], 33: [13, 14, 15], 34: [14, 13, 15], 35: [15, 14, 13], 36: [15, 13, 14] }, 'hosp_prefs': { 13: [29, 30, 33, 31, 32, 34, 35, 36], 14: [31, 32, 34, 29, 30, 33, 35, 36], 15: [35, 36, 31, 32, 29, 30, 33, 34] } } }
- # Solve each block all_block_matchings = {} for block_name, block_data in blocks.items(): matchings = find_block_matchings( block_name, block_data['res'], block_data['hosp'], capacity, block_data['res_prefs'], block_data['hosp_prefs'] ) all_block_matchings[block_name] = matchings print(f"Block {block_name}: {len(matchings)} stable matchings")
- # Combine all blocks total = 1 for block_name, matchings in all_block_matchings.items(): total *= len(matchings)
- print(f"\nTotal stable matchings: {total}") print(f"STATUS: sat") ```

- Actually, I realize I should be more careful about the stability encoding. Let me re-examine.
- For a blocking pair (r, h): 1. r and h are mutually acceptable 2. r prefers h over current match OR r is unmatched 3. h has free capacity OR h prefers r over at least one current assignee
- My encoding: - r_prefers_h = Or(match[r] == 0, Or([match[r] == hp for hp in ... if res_rank[(r,h)] < res_rank[(r,hp)]]))
- Wait, this is wrong. `match[r] == hp` means r is matched to hp. If res_rank[(r,h)] < res_rank[(r,hp)], it means r prefers h over hp. So if r is matched to hp and prefers h over hp, then r wants h.
- But I also need to handle the case where r is matched to a hospital that's NOT in r's preference list. But by construction, match[r] can only be 0 or one of the acceptable hospitals. So this should be fine.
- Let me also think about the case where r is matched to h itself. In that case, (r, h) is not a blocking pair because they're already matched. My encoding handles this because: - r_prefers_h checks if r prefers h over current match. If r is matched to h, then res_rank[(r,h)] is not less than res_rank[(r,h)], so r_prefers_h would only be True if match[r] == 0 (unmatched). But match[r] == h, not 0. So r_prefers_h is False. Good.

Since res_rank[(r,h)] is not less than itself, h is not included. For other hp, if h is preferred over hp, then match[r] == hp would be True only if r is actually matched to hp. But r is matched to h, not hp. So match[r] == hp is False. - r_prefers_h = Or(match[r] == 0, Or(r_prefers_parts)). Since match[r] == h (not 0), and all r_prefers_parts are False, r_prefers_h is False. - So Or(Not(r_prefers_h), Not(h_would_accept)) = Or(True, ...) = True. Good.

- Hmm, actually I want to double-check one thing. The problem says "Find all stable matchings". In the Hospital-Resident problem with incomplete preference lists (some pairs are unacceptable), the set of stable matchings has a lattice structure. The problem asks to enumerate all of them.
- Let me write the script. I'll use the block decomposition for efficiency.
- ```python from z3 import * from itertools import product
- def find_block_matchings(block_name, res_list, hosp_list, cap, res_prefs_block, hosp_prefs_block): solver = Solver()
- match = {} for r in res_list: match[r] = Int(f'match_{r}') acceptable = res_prefs_block.get(r, []) if acceptable: solver.add(Or([match[r] == 0] + [match[r] == h for h in acceptable])) else: solver.add(match[r] == 0)
- for h in hosp_list: acceptable_res = hosp_prefs_block.get(h, []) if acceptable_res: solver.add(Sum([If(match[r] == h, 1, 0) for r in acceptable_res]) <= cap[h])
- res_rank = {} for r in res_list: for i, h in enumerate(res_prefs_block.get(r, [])): res_rank[(r, h)] = i
- hosp_rank = {} for h in hosp_list: for i, r in enumerate(hosp_prefs_block.get(h, [])): hosp_rank[(h, r)] = i
- acceptable_pairs = set() for r in res_list: for h in res_prefs_block.get(r, []): if h in hosp_prefs_block and r in hosp_prefs_block[h]: acceptable_pairs.add((r, h))
- for (r, h) in acceptable_pairs: r_prefers_parts = [] for hp in res_prefs_block.get(r, []): if res_rank[(r, h)] < res_rank.get((r, hp), 999): r_prefers_parts.append(match[r] == hp) r_prefers_h = Or([match[r] == 0] + r_prefers_parts)
- h_acceptable_res = hosp_prefs_block.get(h, []) h_has_capacity = Sum([If(match[rp] == h, 1, 0) for rp in h_acceptable_res]) < cap[h]
- h_prefers_parts = [] for rp in hosp_prefs_block.get(h, []): if hosp_rank[(h, r)] < hosp_rank.get((h, rp), 999): h_prefers_parts.append(match[rp] == h)
- if h_prefers_parts: h_would_accept = Or(h_has_capacity, Or(h_prefers_parts)) else: h_would_accept = h_has_capacity
- solver.add(Or(Not(r_prefers_h), Not(h_would_accept)))
- solutions = [] while solver.check() == sat: m = solver.model() sol = {} for r in res_list: val = m.evaluate(match[r], model_completion=True) sol[r] = int(str(val)) solutions.append(sol) solver.add(Or([match[r] != sol[r] for r in res_list]))
- return solutions
- # ... (block definitions and combination) ```
- Let me now write the full script and run it.
- Wait, I need to think about one more thing. The `Or([match[r] == 0] + r_prefers_parts)` expression. If `r_prefers_parts` is empty (r doesn't prefer any hospital over h), then this becomes `Or([match[r] == 0])` which is just `match[r] == 0`. This means r_prefers_h is True only if r is unmatched. That's correct: if r is matched to some hospital and doesn't prefer h over it, then r doesn't want h.
- But wait, what if r is matched to h itself? Then match[r] == h, not 0. So r_prefers_h is False. Good.
- What if r is matched to some hp where r prefers hp over h? Then match[r] == hp, not 0. And hp is not in r_prefers_parts (because we only include hospitals that r prefers LESS than h). So r_prefers_h is False. Good.
- What if r is matched to some hp where r prefers h over hp? Then match[r] == hp, and hp IS in r_prefers_parts. So r_prefers_h is True. Good.
- OK, the encoding is correct. Let me write the full script.
- Actually, I realize there might be an issue with the `Or` function when the list has only one element. Let me check: `Or([x])` should return `x`. Yes, Z3 handles this correctly.
- And `Or([])` would be... hmm, that's an empty disjunction. In Z3, `Or()` with no arguments returns False. Let me check: `Or([])` - actually, I think Z3's `Or` expects at least one argument. Let me handle this edge case.
- Actually, in the code above, `r_prefers_parts` could be empty, but `Or([match[r] == 0] + r_prefers_parts)` always has at least one element (match[r] == 0). So this is fine.
- For `h_prefers_parts`, I already handle the empty case with the `if h_prefers_parts` check.

- I'll print each matching as a list of [r, h] pairs.
- Let me write the complete script:
- ```python from z3 import * from itertools import product as iter_product
- def find_block_matchings(block_name, res_list, hosp_list, cap, res_prefs_block, hosp_prefs_block): solver = Solver()
- match = {} for r in res_list: match[r] = Int(f'match_{block_name}_{r}') acceptable = res_prefs_block.get(r, []) if acceptable: solver.add(Or([match[r] == 0] + [match[r] == h for h in acceptable])) else: solver.add(match[r] == 0)
- for h in hosp_list: acceptable_res = hosp_prefs_block.get(h, []) if acceptable_res: solver.add(Sum([If(match[r] == h, 1, 0) for r in acceptable_res]) <= cap[h])
- res_rank = {} for r in res_list: for i, h in enumerate(res_prefs_block.get(r, [])): res_rank[(r, h)] = i
- hosp_rank = {} for h in hosp_list: for i, r in enumerate(hosp_prefs_block.get(h, [])): hosp_rank[(h, r)] = i
- acceptable_pairs = set() for r in res_list: for h in res_prefs_block.get(r, []): if h in hosp_prefs_block and r in hosp_prefs_block[h]: acceptable_pairs.add((r, h))
- for (r, h) in acceptable_pairs: r_prefers_parts = [] for hp in res_prefs_block.get(r, []): if res_rank[(r, h)] < res_rank.get((r, hp), 999): r_prefers_parts.append(match[r] == hp) r_prefers_h = Or([match[r] == 0] + r_prefers_parts)
- h_acceptable_res = hosp_prefs_block.get(h, []) h_has_capacity = Sum([If(match[rp] == h, 1, 0) for rp in h_acceptable_res]) < cap[h]
- h_prefers_parts = [] for rp in hosp_prefs_block.get(h, []): if hosp_rank[(h, r)] < hosp_rank.get((h, rp), 999): h_prefers_parts.append(match[rp] == h)
- if h_prefers_parts: h_would_accept = Or(h_has_capacity, Or(h_prefers_parts)) else: h_would_accept = h_has_capacity
- solver.add(Or(Not(r_prefers_h), Not(h_would_accept)))
- solutions = [] while solver.check() == sat: m = solver.model() sol = {} for r in res_list: val = m.evaluate(match[r], model_completion=True) sol[r] = int(str(val)) solutions.append(sol) solver.add(Or([match[r] != sol[r] for r in res_list]))
- return solutions
- capacity = { 1: 2, 2: 2, 3: 2, 4: 2, 5: 2, 6: 2, 7: 4, 8: 3, 9: 1, 10: 3, 11: 3, 12: 2, 13: 3, 14: 3, 15: 2, 16: 2, 17: 2, 18: 1, 19: 1, 20: 1 }
- blocks = { 'A1': { 'res': [1, 2, 3, 4], 'hosp': [1, 2], 'res_prefs': {1: [1, 2], 2: [1, 2], 3: [2, 1], 4: [2, 1]}, 'hosp_prefs': {1: [3, 4, 1, 2], 2: [1, 2, 3, 4]} }, 'A2': { 'res': [5, 6, 7, 8], 'hosp': [3, 4], 'res_prefs': {5: [3, 4], 6: [3, 4], 7: [4, 3], 8: [4, 3]}, 'hosp_prefs': {3: [7, 8, 5, 6], 4: [5, 6, 7, 8]} }, 'A3': { 'res': [9, 10, 11, 12], 'hosp': [5, 6], 'res_prefs': {9: [5, 6], 10: [5, 6], 11: [6, 5], 12: [6, 5]}, 'hosp_prefs': {5: [11, 12, 9, 10], 6: [9, 10, 11, 12]} }, 'A4': { 'res': [37, 38, 39, 40], 'hosp': [16, 17], 'res_prefs': {37: [16, 17], 38: [16, 17], 39: [17, 16], 40: [17, 16]}, 'hosp_prefs': {16: [39, 40, 37, 38], 17: [37, 38, 39, 40]} }, 'B1': { 'res': [13, 14, 15, 16, 17, 18, 19, 20], 'hosp': [7, 8, 9], 'res_prefs': { 13: [7, 8, 9], 14: [7, 8, 9], 15: [8, 7, 9], 16: [8, 7, 9], 17: [7, 8, 9], 18: [7, 9, 8], 19: [8, 9, 7], 20: [9, 8, 7] }, 'hosp_prefs': { 7: [13, 14, 17, 18, 15, 16, 19, 20], 8: [15, 16, 19, 13, 14, 17, 18, 20], 9: [20, 19, 18, 17, 16, 15, 14, 13] } }, 'B2': { 'res': [21, 22, 23, 24, 25, 26, 27, 28], 'hosp': [10, 11, 12], 'res_prefs': { 21: [10, 11, 12], 22: [10, 12, 11], 23: [11, 10, 12], 24: [11, 12, 10], 25: [10, 11, 12], 26: [11, 10, 12], 27: [12, 11, 10], 28: [12, 10, 11] }, 'hosp_prefs': { 10: [21, 22, 25, 23, 24, 26, 27, 28], 11: [23, 24, 26, 21, 22, 25, 27, 28], 12: [27, 28, 23, 24, 21, 22, 25, 26] } }, 'B3': { 'res': [29, 30, 31, 32, 33, 34, 35, 36], 'hosp': [13, 14, 15], 'res_prefs': { 29: [13, 14, 15], 30: [13, 15, 14], 31: [14, 13, 15], 32: [14, 15, 13], 33: [13, 14, 15], 34: [14, 13, 15], 35: [15, 14, 13], 36: [15, 13, 14] }, 'hosp_prefs': { 13: [29, 30, 33, 31, 32, 34, 35, 36], 14: [31, 32, 34, 29, 30, 33, 35, 36], 15: [35, 36, 31, 32, 29, 30, 33, 34] } } }
- # Solve each block all_block_matchings = {} for block_name, block_data in blocks.items(): matchings = find_block_matchings( block_name, block_data['res'], block_data['hosp'], capacity, block_data['res_prefs'], block_data['hosp_prefs'] ) all_block_matchings[block_name] = matchings print(f"Block {block_name}: {len(matchings)} stable matchings")
- # Combine all blocks block_names = list(blocks.keys()) block_matching_lists = [all_block_matchings[b] for b in block_names]
- total = 1 for m in block_matching_lists: total *= len(m)
- print(f"\nTotal stable matchings: {total}") print(f"STATUS: sat")
- # Print all matchings print(f"\n--- All {total} Stable Matchings ---") for idx, combo in enumerate(iter_product(*block_matching_lists)): matching = {} for block_match in combo: matching.update(block_match) # Print as list of [r, h] pairs pairs = [[r, matching[r]] for r in sorted(matching.keys()) if matching[r] != 0] print(f"Matching {idx+1}: {pairs}") ```

- Hmm, actually I realize there might be a subtle issue. When I write `Or([match[r] == 0] + r_prefers_parts)`, if `r_prefers_parts` is empty, this becomes `Or([match[r] == 0])`. In Z3, `Or([expr])` should return `expr`. Let me verify this works.
- Actually, I just realized that Z3's `Or` function might not handle a single-element list correctly. Let me use a helper:

- So all residents must be matched (since total capacity equals number of residents and there's a unique stable matching).
- Resident preferences: - r13: h7 > h8 > h9 - r14: h7 > h8 > h9 - r15: h8 > h7 > h9 - r16: h8 > h7 > h9 - r17: h7 > h8 > h9 - r18: h7 > h9 > h8 - r19: h8 > h9 > h7 - r20: h9 > h8 > h7

- Actually, let me just trust the Z3 solver to find the correct answer. Let me write and run the script.
- Let me finalize the script:
- ```python from z3 import * from itertools import product as iter_product
- def find_block_matchings(block_name, res_list, hosp_list, cap, res_prefs_block, hosp_prefs_block): solver = Solver()
- match = {} for r in res_list: match[r] = Int(f'match_{block_name}_{r}') acceptable = res_prefs_block.get(r, []) if acceptable: solver.add(Or([match[r] == 0] + [match[r] == h for h in acceptable])) else: solver.add(match[r] == 0)
- for h in hosp_list: acceptable_res = hosp_prefs_block.get(h, []) if acceptable_res: solver.add(Sum([If(match[r] == h, 1, 0) for r in acceptable_res]) <= cap[h])
- res_rank = {} for r in res_list: for i, h in enumerate(res_prefs_block.get(r, [])): res_rank[(r, h)] = i
- hosp_rank = {} for h in hosp_list: for i, r in enumerate(hosp_prefs_block.get(h, [])): hosp_rank[(h, r)] = i
- acceptable_pairs = set() for r in res_list: for h in res_prefs_block.get(r, []): if h in hosp_prefs_block and r in hosp_prefs_block[h]: acceptable_pairs.add((r, h))
- for (r, h) in acceptable_pairs: # r prefers h over current match (or is unmatched) r_prefers_parts = [] for hp in res_prefs_block.get(r, []): if res_rank[(r, h)] < res_rank.get((r, hp), 999): r_prefers_parts.append(match[r] == hp) r_prefers_h = Or([match[r] == 0] + r_prefers_parts)
- # h would accept r h_acceptable_res = hosp_prefs_block.get(h, []) h_has_capacity = Sum([If(match[rp] == h, 1, 0) for rp in h_acceptable_res]) < cap[h]
- h_prefers_parts = [] for rp in hosp_prefs_block.get(h, []): if hosp_rank[(h, r)] < hosp_rank.get((h, rp), 999): h_prefers_parts.append(match[rp] == h)
- if h_prefers_parts: h_would_accept = Or(h_has_capacity, Or(h_prefers_parts)) else: h_would_accept = h_has_capacity
- # Not a blocking pair solver.add(Or(Not(r_prefers_h), Not(h_would_accept)))
- solutions = [] while solver.check() == sat: m = solver.model() sol = {} for r in res_list: val = m.evaluate(match[r], model_completion=True) sol[r] = int(str(val)) solutions.append(sol) solver.add(Or([match[r] != sol[r] for r in res_list]))
- return solutions
- capacity = { 1: 2, 2: 2, 3: 2, 4: 2, 5: 2, 6: 2, 7: 4, 8: 3, 9: 1, 10: 3, 11: 3, 12: 2, 13: 3, 14: 3, 15: 2, 16: 2, 17: 2, 18: 1, 19: 1, 20: 1 }
- blocks = { 'A1': { 'res': [1, 2, 3, 4], 'hosp': [1, 2], 'res_prefs': {1: [1, 2], 2: [1, 2], 3: [2, 1], 4: [2, 1]}, 'hosp_prefs': {1: [3, 4, 1, 2], 2: [1, 2, 3, 4]} }, 'A2': { 'res': [5, 6, 7, 8], 'hosp': [3, 4], 'res_prefs': {5: [3, 4], 6: [3, 4], 7: [4, 3], 8: [4, 3]}, 'hosp_prefs': {3: [7, 8, 5, 6], 4: [5, 6, 7, 8]} }, 'A3': { 'res': [9, 10, 11, 12], 'hosp': [5, 6], 'res_prefs': {9: [5, 6], 10: [5, 6], 11: [6, 5], 12: [6, 5]}, 'hosp_prefs': {5: [11, 12, 9, 10], 6: [9, 10, 11, 12]} }, 'A4': { 'res': [37, 38, 39, 40], 'hosp': [16, 17], 'res_prefs': {37: [16, 17], 38: [16, 17], 39: [17, 16], 40: [17, 16]}, 'hosp_prefs': {16: [39, 40, 37, 38], 17: [37, 38, 39, 40]} }, 'B1': { 'res': [13, 14, 15, 16, 17, 18, 19, 20], 'hosp': [7, 8, 9], 'res_prefs': { 13: [7, 8, 9], 14: [7, 8, 9], 15: [8, 7, 9], 16: [8, 7, 9], 17: [7, 8, 9], 18: [7, 9, 8], 19: [8, 9, 7], 20: [9, 8, 7] }, 'hosp_prefs': { 7: [13, 14, 17, 18, 15, 16, 19, 20], 8: [15, 16, 19, 13, 14, 17, 18, 20], 9: [20, 19, 18, 17, 16, 15, 14, 13] } }, 'B2': { 'res': [21, 22, 23, 24, 25, 26, 27, 28], 'hosp': [10, 11, 12], 'res_prefs': { 21: [10, 11, 12], 22: [10, 12, 11], 23: [11, 10, 12], 24: [11, 12, 10], 25: [10, 11, 12], 26: [11, 10, 12], 27: [12, 11, 10], 28: [12, 10, 11] }, 'hosp_prefs': { 10: [21, 22, 25, 23, 24, 26, 27, 28], 11: [23, 24, 26, 21, 22, 25, 27, 28], 12: [27, 28, 23, 24, 21, 22, 25, 26] } }, 'B3': { 'res': [29, 30, 31, 32, 33, 34, 35, 36], 'hosp': [13, 14, 15], 'res_prefs': { 29: [13, 14, 15], 30: [13, 15, 14], 31: [14, 13, 15], 32: [14, 15, 13], 33: [13, 14, 15], 34: [14, 13, 15], 35: [15, 14, 13], 36: [15, 13, 14] }, 'hosp_prefs': { 13: [29, 30, 33, 31, 32, 34, 35, 36], 14: [31, 32, 34, 29, 30, 33, 35, 36], 15: [35, 36, 31, 32, 29, 30, 33, 34] } } }
- # Solve each block all_block_matchings = {} for block_name, block_data in blocks.items(): matchings = find_block_matchings( block_name, block_data['res'], block_data['hosp'], capacity, block_data['res_prefs'], block_data['hosp_prefs'] ) all_block_matchings[block_name] = matchings print(f"Block {block_name}: {len(matchings)} stable matchings")
- # Combine all blocks block_names = list(blocks.keys()) block_matching_lists = [all_block_matchings[b] for b in block_names]
- total = 1 for m in block_matching_lists: total *= len(m)
- print(f"\nTotal stable matchings: {total}") print(f"STATUS: sat")
- # Print all matchings print(f"\n--- All {total} Stable Matchings ---") for idx, combo in enumerate(iter_product(*block_matching_lists)): matching = {} for block_match in combo: matching.update(block_match) pairs = [[r, matching[r]] for r in sorted(matching.keys()) if matching[r] != 0] print(f"Matching {idx+1}: {pairs}") ```

- ```python from z3 import * x = Int('x') Or([x == 0])  # Should this work? ```
- In Z3's Python API, `Or` is defined as: ```python def Or(*args): ... ```
- So `Or([x == 0])` would pass a list as the first argument. Z3's `Or` function checks if the first argument is a list and unpacks it. So `Or([x == 0])` should return `x == 0`.

- ```python def z3_or(exprs): if len(exprs) == 0: return BoolVal(False) elif len(exprs) == 1: return exprs[0] else: return Or(exprs) ```
- Let me use this helper function to be safe.
- Actually, looking at Z3's source code more carefully, the `Or` function in z3.py is:
- ```python def Or(*args): args = _get_args(args) ... ```
- And `_get_args` is: ```python def _get_args(args): if len(args) == 1 and isinstance(args[0], list): return args[0] return list(args) ```
- So `Or([x == 0])` would be unpacked to `[x == 0]`, and then Z3 would handle it as a single-element disjunction, returning `x == 0`. Good.
- And `Or([])` would be unpacked to `[]`, and Z3 would... hmm, I'm not sure what happens with an empty list. Let me check.
- Actually, looking at the Z3 source code: ```python def Or(*args): args = _get_args(args) num = len(args) if num == 0: return BoolVal(False) ... ```
- So `Or([])` returns `BoolVal(False)`. Good.

- This means r_prefers_h is True if: - r is unmatched (match[r] == 0), OR - r is matched to some hospital hp that r prefers less than h
- But wait, what if r is matched to h itself? Then match[r] == h, not 0. And h is not in r_prefers_parts (because we only include hospitals that r prefers LESS than h). So r_prefers_h is False. Good.
- But what if r is matched to some hospital hp that r prefers MORE than h? Then match[r] == hp, not 0. And hp is not in r_prefers_parts (because we only include hospitals that r prefers LESS than h). So r_prefers_h is False. Good.
- And what if r is matched to some hospital hp that r prefers LESS than h? Then match[r] == hp, and hp IS in r_prefers_parts. So r_prefers_h is True. Good.
- And what if r is unmatched? Then match[r] == 0, so r_prefers_h is True. Good.

- ```python h_has_capacity = Sum([If(match[rp] == h, 1, 0) for rp in h_acceptable_res]) < cap[h] ```
- This checks if the number of residents assigned to h is less than h's capacity. This is correct.
- But wait, I'm using `h_acceptable_res = hosp_prefs_block.get(h, [])`. This is the list of residents that h finds acceptable. But what about residents that are not in h's preference list? They can't be assigned to h anyway (by the acceptability constraint). So the sum only counts residents that are acceptable to h. This is correct.

- Let me finalize the script and run it.
- Actually, I want to also think about the `h_prefers_parts` constraint. I wrote:
- ```python h_prefers_parts = [] for rp in hosp_prefs_block.get(h, []): if hosp_rank[(h, r)] < hosp_rank.get((h, rp), 999): h_prefers_parts.append(match[rp] == h) ```
- This creates a list of conditions: for each resident rp that h prefers less than r, check if rp is assigned to h. If any of these conditions is True, it means h has a current assignee that h prefers less than r, so h would accept r.
- But wait, `hosp_rank[(h, r)]` should be defined because r is in h's preference list (since (r, h) is an acceptable pair). And `hosp_rank[(h, rp)]` should be defined because rp is in h's preference list (since we're iterating over h's preference list). So this should be fine.
- OK, let me run the script now.
- Let me write the final script:
- ```python from z3 import * from itertools import product as iter_product
- def find_block_matchings(block_name, res_list, hosp_list, cap, res_prefs_block, hosp_prefs_block): solver = Solver()
- match = {} for r in res_list: match[r] = Int(f'match_{block_name}_{r}') acceptable = res_prefs_block.get(r, []) if acceptable: solver.add(Or([match[r] == 0] + [match[r] == h for h in acceptable])) else: solver.add(match[r] == 0)
- for h in hosp_list: acceptable_res = hosp_prefs_block.get(h, []) if acceptable_res: solver.add(Sum([If(match[r] == h, 1, 0) for r in acceptable_res]) <= cap[h])
- res_rank = {} for r in res_list: for i, h in enumerate(res_prefs_block.get(r, [])): res_rank[(r, h)] = i
- hosp_rank = {} for h in hosp_list: for i, r in enumerate(hosp_prefs_block.get(h, [])): hosp_rank[(h, r)] = i
- acceptable_pairs = set() for r in res_list: for h in res_prefs_block.get(r, []): if h in hosp_prefs_block and r in hosp_prefs_block[h]: acceptable_pairs.add((r, h))
- for (r, h) in acceptable_pairs: r_prefers_parts = [] for hp in res_prefs_block.get(r, []): if res_rank[(r, h)] < res_rank.get((r, hp), 999): r_prefers_parts.append(match[r] == hp) r_prefers_h = Or([match[r] == 0] + r_prefers_parts)
- h_acceptable_res = hosp_prefs_block.get(h, []) h_has_capacity = Sum([If(match[rp] == h, 1, 0) for rp in h_acceptable_res]) < cap[h]
- h_prefers_parts = [] for rp in hosp_prefs_block.get(h, []): if hosp_rank[(h, r)] < hosp_rank.get((h, rp), 999): h_prefers_parts.append(match[rp] == h)
- if h_prefers_parts: h_would_accept = Or(h_has_capacity, Or(h_prefers_parts)) else: h_would_accept = h_has_capacity
- solver.add(Or(Not(r_prefers_h), Not(h_would_accept)))
- solutions = [] while solver.check() == sat: m = solver.model() sol = {} for r in res_list: val = m.evaluate(match[r], model_completion=True) sol[r] = int(str(val)) solutions.append(sol) solver.add(Or([match[r] != sol[r] for r in res_list]))
- return solutions
- capacity = { 1: 2, 2: 2, 3: 2, 4: 2, 5: 2, 6: 2, 7: 4, 8: 3, 9: 1, 10: 3, 11: 3, 12: 2, 13: 3, 14: 3, 15: 2, 16: 2, 17: 2, 18: 1, 19: 1, 20: 1 }
- blocks = { 'A1': { 'res': [1, 2, 3, 4], 'hosp': [1, 2], 'res_prefs': {1: [1, 2], 2: [1, 2], 3: [2, 1], 4: [2, 1]}, 'hosp_prefs': {1: [3, 4, 1, 2], 2: [1, 2, 3, 4]} }, 'A2': { 'res': [5, 6, 7, 8], 'hosp': [3, 4], 'res_prefs': {5: [3, 4], 6: [3, 4], 7: [4, 3], 8: [4, 3]}, 'hosp_prefs': {3: [7, 8, 5, 6], 4: [5, 6, 7, 8]} }, 'A3': { 'res': [9, 10, 11, 12], 'hosp': [5, 6], 'res_prefs': {9: [5, 6], 10: [5, 6], 11: [6, 5], 12: [6, 5]}, 'hosp_prefs': {5: [11, 12, 9, 10], 6: [9, 10, 11, 12]} }, 'A4': { 'res': [37, 38, 39, 40], 'hosp': [16, 17], 'res_prefs': {37: [16, 17], 38: [16, 17], 39: [17, 16], 40: [17, 16]}, 'hosp_prefs': {16: [39, 40, 37, 38], 17: [37, 38, 39, 40]} }, 'B1': { 'res': [13, 14, 15, 16, 17, 18, 19, 20], 'hosp': [7, 8, 9], 'res_prefs': { 13: [7, 8, 9], 14: [7, 8, 9], 15: [8, 7, 9], 16: [8, 7, 9], 17: [7, 8, 9], 18: [7, 9, 8], 19: [8, 9, 7], 20: [9, 8, 7] }, 'hosp_prefs': { 7: [13, 14, 17, 18, 15, 16, 19, 20], 8: [15, 16, 19, 13, 14, 17, 18, 20], 9: [20, 19, 18, 17, 16, 15, 14, 13] } }, 'B2': { 'res': [21, 22, 23, 24, 25, 26, 27, 28], 'hosp': [10, 11, 12], 'res_prefs': { 21: [10, 11, 12], 22: [10, 12, 11], 23: [11, 10, 12], 24: [11, 12, 10], 25: [10, 11, 12], 26: [11, 10, 12], 27: [12, 11, 10], 28: [12, 10, 11] }, 'hosp_prefs': { 10: [21, 22, 25, 23, 24, 26, 27, 28], 11: [23, 24, 26, 21, 22, 25, 27, 28], 12: [27, 28, 23, 24, 21, 22, 25, 26] } }, 'B3': { 'res': [29, 30, 31, 32, 33, 34, 35, 36], 'hosp': [13, 14, 15], 'res_prefs': { 29: [13, 14, 15], 30: [13, 15, 14], 31: [14, 13, 15], 32: [14, 15, 13], 33: [13, 14, 15], 34: [14, 13, 15], 35: [15, 14, 13], 36: [15, 13, 14] }, 'hosp_prefs': { 13: [29, 30, 33, 31, 32, 34, 35, 36], 14: [31, 32, 34, 29, 30, 33, 35, 36], 15: [35, 36, 31, 32, 29, 30, 33, 34] } } }
- # Solve each block all_block_matchings = {} for block_name, block_data in blocks.items(): matchings = find_block_matchings( block_name, block_data['res'], block_data['hosp'], capacity, block_data['res_prefs'], block_data['hosp_prefs'] ) all_block_matchings[block_name] = matchings print(f"Block {block_name}: {len(matchings)} stable matchings")
- # Combine all blocks block_names = list(blocks.keys()) block_matching_lists = [all_block_matchings[b] for b in block_names]
- total = 1 for m in block_matching_lists: total *= len(m)
- print(f"\nTotal stable matchings: {total}") print(f"STATUS: sat")
- # Print all matchings print(f"\n--- All {total} Stable Matchings ---") for idx, combo in enumerate(iter_product(*block_matching_lists)): matching = {} for block_match in combo: matching.update(block_match) pairs = [[r, matching[r]] for r in sorted(matching.keys()) if matching[r] != 0] print(f"Matching {idx+1}: {pairs}") ```

This is correct because if h has no residents it prefers less than r, then h would only accept r if there's room.

So h_would_accept = h_has_capacity = True. This means h would accept r. This is correct: if h is empty, h would accept any acceptable resident.

- And `Sum(...) < cap[h]` should work. Z3's `<` operator is overloaded for Int expressions.

- If the list is empty, `Or([])` returns `BoolVal(False)`. This is correct: if there are no hospitals that r prefers less than h, then r doesn't prefer h over any current match (except if r is unmatched).

Looking at this problem, I need to:
1. Model the Hospital-Resident matching with capacities using Z3
2. Encode stability (no blocking pairs)
3. Enumerate all stable matchings by exploiting the independent block structure

stable matchings for an independent block.\"\"\"\n    solver = Solver()\n    \n    # Decision variables: match[r] = hospital assigned to resident r (0 = unmatched)\n    match = {}\n    for r in in acceptable]))\n        else:\n            solver.add(match[r] == 0)\n    \n    # Capacity constraints\n    for h in hosp_list:\n        acceptable_res = hosp_prefs_block.get(h, [])\n        if in res_list:\n        for i, h in enumerate(res_prefs_block.get(r, [])):\n            res_rank[(r, h)] = i\n    \n    hosp_rank = {}\n    for h in hosp_list:\n        for i, r in would accept r (free capacity OR prefers r over some assignee)\n        h_acceptable_res = hosp_prefs_block.get(h, [])\n        h_has_capacity = Sum([If(match[rp] == h, 1, 0) for rp in h_has_capacity\n        \n        # Not a blocking pair: ~(r_prefers_h AND h_would_accept)\n        solver.add(Or(Not(r_prefers_h), Not(h_would_accept)))\n    \n    # Enumerate all solutions\n sol[r] = int(str(val))\n        solutions.append(sol)\n        # Block this solution\n        solver.add(Or([match[r] != sol[r] for r in res_list]))\n    \n    return solutions\n\n# Hospital
